In his tent, soft languid sounds<br>  Expiring on her falling lute, arose<br>  To welcome home her Lord his beauteous slave; [320]<br>  His slave!  is that her slavery, round his neck<br>  The snowy girdle of her arms to wreathe?<br>  To catch a master's mandate doth she raise<br>  The bashful fringes of her eyes, and meet<br>  Those glances of no lordly scorn, that soothe [325]<br>  Her gentle wayward angriness of love,<br>  Soothe, dare not chide, that coldness faint and brief<br>  That would be wooed, but sweeter to be won?<br>  Nor dares not she withhold that arm uprais'd<br>  From their high stand the furniture of fight, [330]<br>  Glaive, corslet, morion to displace; her touch<br>  Now clings with soft resistance, playful now<br>  Thwarts his stern purpose. -- "Oh, remove not them;<br>  In hours of absence, thou too dearly lov'st,<br>  They are my comfort, my companions they, [335]<br>  My all but thou: the dusky shades of eve<br>  Brown o'er their glittering steal, and there array,<br>  A bright and armed man, th' officious air<br>  Gives motion, and with all thy graceful pride<br>  Shakes the light plumage, thou art there, in spite [340]<br>  Of thy own tardy lingering, thou art there.<br>  Oh, I have woke at midnight, when my soul<br>  With thee hath been a wanderer through sad fields,<br>  'Mid death and battle, though my lightest touch<br>  Had prov'd thee by my side, yet my faint hand [345]<br>  Lack'd courage with that dangerous proof to front<br>  My unsubstantial fears.  Oh then, if light<br>  Of star or moon on their blue surface gleam'd,<br>  Or wind awoke them into sound, again<br>  Calm on my pillow droop'd my cheek to rest, [350]<br>  Secure to find thee sweetly slumbering there.<br>  Yet, yet unwon, oh, lighten that cold brow,<br>  And I will sing the soft and sleepy song<br>  That makes a woman of thy angry eyes,<br>  Lulls the rude tumult in thy troubled breast, [355]<br>  Leaving nought there but melody and me."<br>  <br>  Then started she to feel how hard and cold<br>  Between her and her bosom's resting place<br>  The corslet lay, by stealth her fond embrace<br>  Supplanting; gently his one arm declin'd [360]<br>  Over her neck, in careless fondness hangs,<br>  Busy the other, its rude office frames<br>  Linking the breastplate's clasps; now holds he back<br>  From her approaching lips his cheek, to fix<br>  The weighty morion; but her garrulous grief [365]<br>  Paus'd not -- "At midnight! now! oh brave misdeem'd,<br>  Misdeem'd, who only th' open day would front<br>  With his bold armour; who but I would love,<br>  I, weak and brainsick, one whose valour shrouds<br>  Its prowess in the cloudy gloom of night? [370]<br>  Oh not, oh not to war, thou goest to win<br>  Some lovelier or some newer bride.  Go, go,<br>  Though faithless, barbarous, cruel, cold to me,<br>  Yet make not her too wretched, make not her<br>  Heartsick with sad expectance." -- But her arms [375]<br>  Belied her desperate language, closer clasp'd<br>  With more than maiden strength.  "Oh, stony heart,<br>  And I for thee forsook my infant home,<br>  Where all my steps were music, all my smiles<br>  Glad sunshine to my parents wintry blood, [380]<br>  That glanc'd like summer waters at my sight:<br>  For thee did violence to my virgin fame:<br>  By war's rude force might I have seem'd enthrall'd,<br>  A luckless, pitied damsel; my fond heart<br>  Ill brook'd the coarse reproach of ravisher [385]<br>  Should couple with a name so dear as thine.<br>  At night-fall fled I to thee; even as now<br>  The stars shone beauteous, and a kindly gloom<br>  Curtain'd our meeting even as now; no change<br>  From soft and fond and gentle, but in thee." -- [390]<br>  "Peace, trembler, peace! to-morrow's dawn shall hail,<br>  Borne in the shield of honour, on the necks<br>  Of his tall peers, thy Abisa; no voice<br>  Silent, no quiet in the troubled air,<br>  Restless with his hymn'd triumph, Offa's heart [395]<br>  Sick with wan envy.  Then, Myfanwy, then<br>  My glory shall make rapture of thy tears,<br>  And thou shalt bless the grief that wrings thee now."<br>  "Oh, glory hath a stern and savage mate,<br>  Danger, her lawless paramour, enfolds [400]<br>  Her beauties in his churlish arms.  Oh pause,<br>  And yet farewell, 'tis exquisite to part,<br>  For oh, thou weep'st at parting, 'twast past hope<br>  To see a tear on that stern face for me." --<br>  <br>  She hath her last cold kiss through the barr'd helm<br>  Won hardly; she is calm as though it dwelt [406]<br>  Yet on her lips, she hears his parting steps,<br>  Yet lingers on her cheek that liquid glow,<br>  That brilliant harmony of smile and tear<br>  That at the presence of the one belov'd [410]<br>  Flits o'er the settled purple of the cheek.<br>  Oh, if soft woman hath her wilder fears,<br>  She hath her wilder hopes, for man's stern grasp<br>  Too thin, too airy!  "Never yet found false,<br>  Thou wilt return;" (so wanton'd her gay dreams) [415]<br>  "So young, so lovely, fate would shame to snatch<br>  So early the choice glories of the earth." --<br>  Then sate she down triumphal coronets<br>  To weave, but not in modest quiet grief,<br>  And gentle resignation pale and mild, [420]<br>  But with a dancing heart and bright blithe eye;<br>  And when her eyelids droop'd, soft o'er her came<br>  A sweet inconstant slumber, such as sleep<br>  Love-dreaming maidens ere their bridal morn.<br>  <br>  But through the clear calm night, the azure plain<br>  Of heaven, with all its glittering paths of light [426]<br>  Distinct and dazzling, mov'd that fair-hair'd youth;<br>  So, if old fable may be won to smile<br>  Its grace upon our darker tale, the boy,<br>  Smooth-cheek'd Endymion, his enamour'd Moon [430]<br>  Woo'd with no lawless witchcraft from her sphere:<br>  Nor she delay'd, her silver-sandal'd feet<br>  Gliding and glancing o'er the dews she came,<br>  And curtain'd in a cloud of snowy light,<br>  Mock'd mortal harps that hymn'd her cold and chaste.<br>  No amorous fancies o'er thy downless cheek [436]<br>  Flushing their rosy heat, no love-lipp'd tones<br>  In sweet disturbance stealing on the air,<br>  Young Abisa!  with more imperious charm<br>  Thou summon'st from wild wood or cavern'd heath, [440]<br>  Nor vainly, their fierce habitant.  Behold,<br>  A shadow by thine own, its stately length<br>  On the white dews advancing; at thy side<br>  The Avenger, as upsprung from nether earth.<br>  <br>  Then fatal gladness leap'd in that young heart, [445]<br>  He flung his vizor'd helmet proudly up,<br>  And dash'd defiance 'gainst fierce Offa's dread.<br>  <br>  But Samor, for when his pure heart was wean'd<br>  From all the faint and feeble of his kind,<br>  The mercies clung within, and gentleness [450]<br>  So mingled with his nature, that it slaked<br>  Even the blood-thirsting phrenzy of revenge;<br>  Samor that beauteous youth survey'd, the stars<br>  Glimmer'd a blue and hazy light, that shewed<br>  His soft locks spreading their bright clusters wide, [455]<br>  His vermeil cheek most lovely in its wrath,<br>  And brow that seem'd to wonder and delight<br>  At its own dauntlessness.  So tall, so fair;<br>  Oft had he imag'd his own perish'd boy<br>  In flower of youth, that flower which never bloom'd. [460]<br>  Tender and mild his voice, as though he spake<br>  Even to that dead belov'd -- "Oh, brave and fair,<br>  Why thus abroad amid the silent night,<br>  With menace and fierce gesture wild and strange?"<br>  "Thou heardst my call, thou seest my arms, my aim [465]<br>  Idly thou question'st." -- "Tis not, gentle youth,<br>  Thy golden luxury of hair, nor cheek<br>  Warm in the rosy wantonness of youth,<br>  But thy brave bearing, gallant mien and proud,<br>  That winds long-banish'd mercy round my sword, [470]<br>  To save from it one Saxon life." -- "Soft praise,<br>  And sweet from lady's lips, but not to hear<br>  Smooth Flattery's descant come I, but to win<br>  What, being won, is in its lofty self<br>  Imperishable beauty, garlands youth [475]<br>  With honour passing the white hairs of age,<br>  Glory, the life of life." -- "And is there none<br>  Whose pillow dreams of thee are haunting now?<br>  No mother, whose last waking thought was hope,<br>  At morn, to meet thee in thy wonted glow [480]<br>  Of loveliness and life?  No gentle maid<br>  Whom the bare thought of paleness in thy cheek,<br>  Of death's wan chill upon thy brow, would waste<br>  And wither like the canker'd flower of spring?<br>  Return to her, oh fair, high-minded youth! [485]<br>  Ere yet too late, return." -- But more delay<br>  The hot youth brook'd not; down he clasp'd his helm<br>  And leaping to the frantic onset, cried,<br>  Now, Offa, for thy shame, and for thy meed,<br>  My brother Hengist!" -- As when lightning flame [490]<br>  Dashes at midnight o'er his slumbering lids,<br>  Up starts the wild steed, all his tawny mane<br>  Bristling and blazing, he devours the earth<br>  In fury; even so sudden those rash words<br>  Set flames upon the Avenger's brow, set wrath [495]<br>  On the impetuous motion of his spear.<br>  <br>  Oh, holy Night!  in thy injurious gloom<br>  How blank the proud distinctions of man's fame!<br>  Languor and loftiness, and shame and pride<br>  In one dead darkness, deep forgetfulness, [500]<br>  Lie, as within a grave, till Virtue's self,<br>  But for her haughty consciousness within,<br>  Might weary of her mute and viewless deeds.<br>  Secret and still, that I might violate<br>  Thy mysteries, and redeem from envious gloom [505]<br>  That Saxon boy's dead honours, dearly won,<br>  Most dearly, yet most nobly.  Morn shall tell<br>  The issue of that conflict, but no morn<br>  Will dawn upon his silent, perish'd praise.<br>  <br>  Two hours are past, alone the Avenger moves [510]<br>  Under the stars of heaven; 'tis midnight deep,<br>  Now comes his hour of softness; love-sick boy,<br>  Tuning soft phrenzies to his wanton lute,<br>  Is not more wild, fantastical, or fond,<br>  Than Britain's stately hope, high Hengist's dread. [515]<br>  For ever at this hour, of parted joy<br>  Dim gleams revisit his forsaken soul,<br>  Like once-lov'd music o'er a maniac's ear,<br>  Faintly and feebly sweet, the dead put on<br>  Their earthly lustre, Emeric comes, as fair [520]<br>  As from the bridal altar, but less coy,<br>  In fervent full abandonment of love.<br>  The breezes are melodious with her voice,<br>  The dews are printed by her slender feet,<br>  She flows into his arms, her fond embrace [525]<br>  Is warm upon his soul.  Thus aye she comes,<br>  Or when 'tis wintry in the starless skies,<br>  Or when the moonlight bathes the earth, to her<br>  Heaven opes its crystal portals, beauteous light<br>  Ushers her presence, sleep can ne'er estrange [530]<br>  That luxury from his heart; when consciousness<br>  Of all things earthly slumbereth and is dead,<br>  She haunts within, her sweet intrusion clings<br>  To the lull'd spirit, senseless but to her,<br>  All, all the living of the man is her's. [535]<br>  <br>  Oh, in their dreamings, their communions wild<br>  With airy, immaterial visitants,<br>  Most differ Guilt and Virtue; there are shapes<br>  Hideous and hateful, snaky Gorgon smiles,<br>  And all the fabled populace of hell, [540]<br>  Brooding disquiet o'er the thorny couch;<br>  But Virtue's visions are almost as fair<br>  As Angels blest realities; to thee<br>  Lovely thy nightly visitant, sad Chief!<br>  As to man, sinless yet in Eden's bowers, [545]<br>  On beds of odorous amaranth asleep,<br>  Yet uncreated, came his virgin bride,<br>  Delicate phantom; then his fresh pure soul<br>  Amorous enchantment, first entranc'd, first rose<br>  That our best feeling, of lost Paradise [450]<br>  That sole surviving pleasure, holy love.<br>  <br>  Beauteous thy blue uprising, mist-rob'd Morn;<br>  All thy bright glittering of fantastic dews<br>  With their thin tissue silkening the green meads,<br>  And all thy music of blithe leaves that dance [555]<br>  In the caressing breeze, and matins gay<br>  From all the living woodland, Sleep is pleas'd<br>  To be so sweetly banish'd her soft reign.<br>  But dreary are thy sounds, and sad thy light<br>  On the lewd wassail, riots orgies rude,<br>  Polluting day with sights that shame dark night.<br>  <br>  Now from the state pavilion forth are pour'd<br>  The synod of high banqueters, their eyes<br>  Hot with loose raptures and distemper'd joy,<br>  Voluptuously turbulent their souls. [565]<br>  Right in their way stood fix'd a lofty spear,<br>  Not with gay garland crown'd, or streaming silk,<br>  But, with that beauteous head that yesternight<br>  Confronted them with graceful pride; the cheek<br>  Where wantonly youth's rosy banner gleam'd, [570]<br>  Pale, dewy, stiffening, lifeless, lustreless;<br>  Part matted with red damp the golden locks<br>  Clung round the spear, part curling on the air,<br>  Sad semblance shew'd of life, in all the rest<br>  Making the stillness and fix'd cold more dread. [575]<br>  <br>  No cheek was there so bright, voluptuous heart<br>  So hot, but, like bleak snow, fear fell on it<br>  With a cold thrill and searching; if their sight<br>  Had yet perception, humbler chiefs might draw<br>  From high example comfort for their dread; [580]<br>  Brow might they see with kingly crown beset,<br>   White, sad, and shrunken as their own.  Alone,<br>  Fierce smil'd the pride of Offa; he held up<br>  To those wan lips the sparkling shell of mead:<br>  "Drink, thou hast kept thy oath, drink, soft-lipp'd boy!"<br>  <br>  O'er all the camp spread loud and wide and far [586]<br>  The name of Abisa; Myfanwy heard<br>  Where lay she dreaming half, and fabling half<br>  Of garlands and of gay triumphal pomp.<br>  How nimble are the feet that bear light hearts. [590]<br>  She is gone forth, and all for joy forgot<br>  The veil e'er wont to dim her dazzling cheek,<br>  Forgot the braiding of her hair, the maid<br>  So soft, so timorous, at the wanton breeze<br>  She oft hath trembled, 'neath day's eye retired [595]<br>  Even from the fondness of her own loved youth.<br>  Through files of warriors, who uncasque their brows<br>  To fill their curious gaze, she hurries on,<br>  She knows not what she sees, and only knows,<br>  She sees not what she seeks, that cheek, that eye [600]<br>  Which fed on her with such excess of love<br>  As if 'twere worse than blindness to lose sight<br>  Of its sole idol; only she is blithe,<br>  She only smiling 'mid those many sad.<br>  She meets even all she longs for; up from earth [605]<br>  (For now from that sad eminence of scorn<br>  Had friendly hand remov'd it, now had cleans'd<br>  Its damp defilement) that dear face on her<br>  Settled its fixed and inexpressive gaze.<br>  Her mien was strangely rational, her look [610]<br>  Like one that calmly ponder'd what it saw,<br>  Her voice articulate and passionless.<br>  "What hath done this?" -- "The Avenger, the unknown,"<br>  Spake many voices. -- "Oh, my hands are weak;<br>  Ye see them soft and delicate and white, [615]<br>  But thou, and thou, and thou, art bold and strong,<br>  And bear'st bright armour, ye will sure requite<br>  The slaughter on the slaughter's head." -- Ensued<br>  Brief moments of a stagnant grief, life paus'd,<br>  As 'twould prolong unconsciousness, delay [620]<br>  Yet, yet that state that wakes with waking sense.<br>  Then kindled up her eye, but not with joy,<br>  Then flush'd her cheek a light and sanguine red,<br>  That is fair marble flitted o'er, but left<br>  Nor tinge nor warmth; she snatch'd up to her heart<br>  That lifeless thing and fled; as some fond bird [626]<br>  With spread wings hovering o'er her nest, looks round<br>  At some black shape of fear, then turns to see<br>  If yet her callow brood are slumbering safe,<br>  So wandering her dim eye on all around, [630]<br>  Anon with full intensity of love,<br>  Settled on her cold care.  She reach'd the tent,<br>  There miserly her treasure she o'erbroods;<br>  She lays it on her lap, and sings to it,<br>  Now gazes as she thought even yet those eyes [635]<br>  Might open, those wan lips their wonted sounds<br>  Murmur, now almost sees a forming smile:<br>  Now gaily carols on her broken songs,<br>  Ever his favourite, most familiar tones,<br>  And now breaks off, as fearful to disturb [640]<br>  His quiet slumbers, only speaks in smiles,<br>  Language by him e'er understood, and once,<br>  Once her rash lips approach'd: so pass'd the hours<br>  From earliest morning till the setting sun.<br>  Then that wild spirit and playfulness of grief [645]<br>  Sadden'd to drear sobriety, gave place<br>  Sweet-dreaming twilight to the bright clear day.<br>  Then first she thought of beasts and fowls obscene<br>  Battening on his fair limbs, no hand to heap<br>  The scanty pity of a little earth [650]<br>  Upon the brave, the princely, and the fair:<br>  Envious of partner in her sacred toil,<br>  Bearing her cold wan burthen in her arms,<br>  Alone upon the pious quest she speeds.<br>  She fears not, ah too wretched now to fear! [655]<br>  Darkness is on her steps, but what to her<br>  Though nature's rich varieties are blank?<br>  Her guide the unblinded sympathies within;<br>  The love that link'd her to his living soul<br>  Will light her to him lifeless; yon wan stars, [660]<br>  That struggle with the haze, are bright enough<br>  To beam upon the dead.  But now more fast<br>  Their golden cressets multiply, more clear,<br>  And lo fierce Offa in her path: his eye<br>  Fix'd on her with a rude imperious lust, [665]<br>  As the pollution of his bad desires<br>  Did honour to their victim.  But the maid,<br>  Unbelieving, unsuspecting aught impure,<br>  With sweet beseeching, almost with caress,<br>  Would win her onward passage; when her soul [670]<br>  Was startled into fear, she would not think,<br>  Such savage nature dwelt in human hearts.<br>  She wept, she sued, she drew the veil away,<br>  Upheld that lovely lifeless thing -- in vain:<br>  The snowy dove is in the rude kite's grasp, [675]<br>  Pale, fluttering, fainting; upon Heaven she call'd,<br>  Cruelly calm look'd on her the cool skies;<br>  She call'd on Abisa, but only felt<br>  More deeply that cold glassiness of face,<br>  That dull, indifferent witness of her shame; [680]<br>  But in the stress and hurry of despair<br>  Strange energies were hers, with frantic voice<br>  She call'd on the Avenger -- Lo, he comes,<br>  Terrible in the silence of his arms,<br>  And earth is dank with Offa's lustful blood. [685]<br>  But her first motion was a frantic kiss<br>  On Abisa's cold lips, as though for him<br>  Proud of the untainted treasure of her love;<br>  Then turn'd to her preserver, but with looks<br>  Of loathing more than thankfulness; he stood [690]<br>  In gentle majesty serene, yet proud<br>  Of that light victory, of prevented crime<br>  Severely joyful; bitter strife of heart<br>  Spake in her language -- "Had it been but death,<br>  I yet had curs'd thee!  oh, look here, look here! [695]<br>  (And she withdrew the clust'ring curls that veil'd<br>  The rigid deathfulness of that fair brow)<br>  Oh, one sole feeling to this dead heart seem'd<br>  A duty and delight, the hate of thee.<br>  Cruel, even that thou enviest me, even that." -- [700]<br>  "That, British maiden! is a Saxon's face,<br>  Yet mourns thy amorous heart in guilty tears?"<br>  "Is there not beauty in a Saxon's cheek,<br>  Is there not music on a Saxon's tongue,<br>  Is there not tenderness in Saxon hearts? [705]<br>  Oh, he is kind and true, his love to me<br>  Almost as deep and fond, as mine to him,<br>  Wild that I am, he was, that fatal was<br>  Makes agony my sacred thought of him." --<br>  "Maiden, by Wye's transparent stream abode [710]<br>  An aged pair, and their declining day<br>  One beauteous child enlighten'd, and dispens'd<br>  Soft moonlight o'er their darkening eve; they thought<br>  The only pang of death from her to part.<br>  But heavy was their sinking to the grave, [715]<br>  For that fair beam in unchaste darkness quench'd<br>  Its virgin lustre, and its light withdrew,<br>  Of their old limbs of life: alone they dwelt,<br>  In discontent and cold distaste of all,<br>  As her ingratitude had made them sick [720]<br>  Of the world's hollowness, and if she fail'd<br>  All earthly things must needs be false and frail.<br>  They ne'er reproach'd her, for so near the grave<br>  They could not hate; but for her sake they loath'd<br>  Each old familiar face, that once they lov'd. [725]<br>  Where she was wont to wander, wander'd they;<br>  The garden flowers she tended, they bound up<br>  With woeful care; their chill and shaking hands<br>  Made tremulous music with her lute, I shrunk<br>  In hoary age to see such childish joys. [730]<br>  They felt one after pleasure, the same hour<br>  They glided from their woes, their parting breath,<br>  Blended in languid blessings on her head,<br>  For her went suppliant to the throne of God,<br>  Their lost Myfanwy." -- Trembling stood she there, [735]<br>  Like one that strives to weep, but the hard tears<br>  Are frozen in their source. "Oh thou are I,<br>  Sweet Abisa (to that cold head she spake),<br>  We will go weep upon their graves, and win<br>  Their spirits to forgiveness; when they hear [740]<br>  How fervent and how fatal were our loves,<br>  Heaven will lend airs to waft their mercy down."<br>  "Fond Maid, beware! repentance must be chaste<br>  And spotless as the unsunn'd snow; wilt thou<br>  Yet wanton with the memory of thy sin, [745]<br>  Bad thoughts at revel in thy heart, with vows<br>  Lightly made up of guilty breath impure,<br>  Pollute and sicken the clear air that dwells<br>  About the holy dwellings of the dead;<br>  Waver from God to Pagan paramour [750]<br>  With wandering loose affections." "Hard and cold,"<br>  Be thou content to have robb'd this widow'd heart<br>  Of that most lovely breathing thing earth bore,<br>  But spare, oh spare, the sinless, senseless dead!<br>  Cruel, by yon bright stars I oft have sworn [755]<br>  Ne'er to forego him; shall I crown my sins<br>  With perjury?  I will weep, and fast, and pray,<br>  And wear the rough stones with my tender knees,<br>  So thou wilt leave me my sad thoughts of him.<br>  Oh, God hath grace for all; my earliest prayer [760]<br>  Shall be for mercy on his perish'd soul,<br>  The next for those who dying pray'd for me,<br>  And for my sad and sinful self the last."<br>  <br>  Most exquisite sorcery of womankind!<br>  Even to the fall'n some cherish'd loveliness [765]<br>  Yet clings, with innocent hypocrisy<br>  Tricking their failures in such tender hues,<br>  We blame with tears, enamour'd while we blame.<br>  Even thus her fervent constancy of love<br>  Brighten'd that guilty maiden. -- "God will weigh [770]<br>  With righteous hand thy sorrows and thy sins,<br>  Damsel, I nor absolve thee, nor condemn.<br>  Come thou with me, and we will reunite<br>  That beauteous boy's remains; oh thou, even thou,<br>  Knewst thou the studious cruelties, cold crimes [775]<br>  By these barbarians wrought on this sad land,<br>  Wouldst pardon this dishonour to the corpse<br>  Of that brave youth." -- She leap'd up to his neck,<br>  "And who are thou, that doest such savage deeds,<br>  Yet forcest us to love thee?" -- On they past, [780]<br>  They reach'd the place of death, he dug away<br>  The earth that fenc'd from wandering kite and wolf<br>  Young Abisa's fair limbs; he sooth'd her woes<br>  By soft participation, her consol'd<br>  By suffering, and the Christian's voice rose up [785]<br>  In prayers for mercy on a Saxon's soul.<br>  <br>  <br>  <b> <h3 align="CENTER">BOOK VII.</h3> </b>   How measureless to erring human sight<br>  Is glory!  Glorious thy majestic state,<br>  Hengist!  with captive cities for thy thrones,<br>  And captive nations thy pale satellites,<br>  Britain, with all her beauty, power, and wealth, [5]<br>  Thy palace of dominion.  Glorious thou,<br>  Caswallon, in Caer Ebranc's stately courts,<br>  By the slow waters of the wandering Ouse,<br>  Bright-sceptred Renegade!  Even in your crimes<br>  Glitters a dazzling and meteorous pomp, [10]<br>  Though your wild voyage hath lain through waves of blood.<br>  Ye ride triumphant in your royal port;<br>  But he, sad Pilgrim, outcast and forlorn<br>  How doth the midnight of his honour shame<br>  Your broad meridian, his wild freedom pass [15]<br>  Your plenitude of sway, his nakedness<br>  Transcend your sweeping purples, rayed with gold!<br>  Nor wanteth to his state its gorgeous pride,<br>  And high peculiar majesty; the pomp<br>  Of the conspiring elements sheds on him [20]<br>  Tumultuous grandeurs; o'er his midnight couch,<br>  Amid the scath'd oaks of the mountain moor,<br>  On its broad wings of gloom the tempest stoops.<br>  Around his head in crystal coronets<br>  The lightning falls, as though thy fiery hand, [25]<br>  Almighty!  through the rolling clouds put forth,<br>  Did honour to the Freeman.  Mighty winds<br>  And the careering thunders spread around<br>  Turbulent music; darkness rivals day,<br>  And day with darkness vies in stateliest pride [30]<br>  The Avenger's lofty miseries to array.<br>  When from the East forth leaps the warrior Sun<br>  In panoply of golden light, dark cowers<br>  His own proud eagle, marvelling what strong form,<br>  Uprising to usurp his haughty right, [35]<br>  Drinks in the intense magnificence with brow<br>  Undazzled and unshrinking; nor to him<br>  Fails homage from the living shapes of earth:<br>  On him the savage, fierce and monstrous, fawn<br>  Tame adoration; from his rugged sleep [40]<br>  The wild boar, sleek his bristling wrath, aloof<br>  Shrinks, the grim wolf no more his rest disturbs,<br>  Than the calm motion of the moon she bays.<br>  <br>  Now, by her native sylvan Wye, that Maid,<br>  Left to cold penitence and prayer, again [45]<br>  Sets forth the high Avenger: now his path<br>  Through Towey's vale winds velvet soft and green.<br>  The year is in its waning autumn glow,<br>  But the warm Sun, with all his summer love,<br>  Hangs o'er this gentle valley, loath to part [50]<br>  From the blue stream that to his amorous beams<br>  Now her cool bosom spreads, now coyer slides<br>  Under her alder shade, whose umbrage green,<br>  Glancing and breaking the fantastic rays,<br>  The deep dark mirror frets with mazy light. [55]<br>  A day that seems in its rich noon to blend<br>  All seasons choice deliciousness, high hung<br>  On Dinevaur and Carreg Cennon rude,<br>  And on bold Drusslyn gleam'd the woods their hues,<br>  Changeful and brilliant, as their leaves had drank [60]<br>  The sun's empyreal fountains; not more bright<br>  The groves of those Atlantic Isles, where rove<br>  (Dream'd elder Poesy such fancies sweet)<br>  The spirits of the brave, stern Peleus' son,<br>  And Diomede, through bowers that the blue air [65]<br>  Arch'd with immortal spring of fragrant gold.<br>  The merry birds, as though they had o'erdream'd<br>  The churlish winter, spring-tide virelays<br>  Carolling, pruned their all-forgotten plumes.<br>  Upon the sunny shallow lay the trout [70]<br>  Kindling the soft gems of its skin; the snake<br>  As fresh and wanton in its green attire<br>  Wound its gay rings along the flowery sward.<br>  <br>  That overpowering beauty in mild bonds<br>  Of sweet amazement and infatuate bliss, [75]<br>  Took prisoner Samor's spirit.  On a rock,<br>  'Neath a white canopy of glistening birch,<br>  He lay surrender'd.  The thin whispering leaves,<br>  The welling waters flow, the lingering, long,<br>  Love-dwelling descant of the joyous birds [80]<br>  Came mingling with the languor of his sense,<br>  Most soothing each in turn, most slumb'ring soft.<br>  <br>  'Tis no harsh breaking in that train of sound<br>  Delicious, but a low and measur'd dash<br>  That blends and deepens all the mingling tones; [85]<br>  'Tis nought to cloud of dim that slow intrudes<br>  On the universal brilliance, crowning all<br>  Moves the gay apparition, and fires up<br>  The restless glittering of intenser blaze.<br>  <br>  Slow up the tide the gaudy bark comes on, [90]<br>  Her oars scarce startling the unruffled air;<br>  The waters to her swan-like prow give place,<br>  Along the oar-blades leap up to the sun<br>  In lucid flakes, and dance, as 'twere their sport<br>  To waft that beauteous freight.  And exquisite [95]<br>  As that voluptuous Memphian on the stream<br>  Of Cydnus, leading with bliss-breathing smiles<br>  Her throngs of rash beholders, glided down<br>  To welcome to his soft imprisonment<br>  The Lord of half the world, so wond'rous fair [100]<br>  Under an awning cool of fluttering silk<br>  The Lady of that graceful galley sate.<br>  But not in her instinct the melting form<br>  With passion, the smooth limbs in dazzling glow<br>  Translucent through the thin lascivious veil, [105]<br>  Skilful with careless blandishments to fire<br>  The loose imaginations, she herein<br>  Least like the Oriental harlot Queen.<br>  Of all her shape, of all her soul was pride<br>  The sustenance, the luxury, the life. [110]<br>  The innate scorn of her full eye repaid<br>  With lofty thanklessness the homage fawn'd<br>  By her fair handmaids, and her oarmen gay,<br>  Who seem'd to wanton in their servile toil.<br>  Around she gaz'd, as in her haughtiness [115]<br>  She thought that God had form'd this living pomp<br>  Of woodland, stream, and rock, her height of soul<br>  To pamper, that to welcome her to earth<br>  Attired its breathing brightness, and the sun<br>  Only on her look'd from his azure sphere. [120]<br>  <br>  Knows Samor that bright Lady?  Who knows not<br>  Amid her twinkling retinue of stars<br>  The queenly summer moon?  Ye too he knows,<br>  The minion rowers of her royal state,<br>  Entitled once by courteous falsehoods bland [125]<br>  Nobles of Britain, from the general wreck<br>  Most despicably saved by Saxon scorn,<br>  Meet vassalage for Vortigern, now shrunk<br>  And dwindled from proud Britain's sov'reign lord<br>  To petty Prince of Dyfed. Ye yet cling [NOTE 12]<br>  Even to the hollow semblance of a crown.<br>  Ye gauzy summer motes, that float and bask<br>  In the warm noontide of a court, light things<br>  Of noise and glittering, that to royal ears<br>  Tinkle your poisonous flatteries, then most proud [135]<br>  When most obtrusive your gay nothingness.<br>  <br>  Under a rock where Samor lay unseen<br>  Beneath the sparkling birchen shade, the bark<br>  Glided so near, the silver-twinkling leaves<br>  Play'd like a wavering veil o'er the bright face [140]<br>  And marble neck of that reclining Queen.<br>  <br>  Now, Samor, now 'tis at thy thirsty lips<br>  The cup of vengeance, now quaff deep, quaff deep!<br>  Now, by the bones that bleach on Ambri plain,<br>  By thy lost Emeric's silent chamber bowers, [145]<br>  By that soft cheek o'er which the primrose blooms,<br>  Now launch the unerring javelin! lo she tempts,<br>  The Saxon's daughter, and the false King's bride,<br>  The tame and baffled lingering of revenge.<br>  <br>  And up the Avenger stood, a ray of light [150]<br>  Quiver'd the brandish'd javelin, creeping awe<br>  Froze up the rowers hearts, down fell the oars,<br>  And to the shore round swung the ungovern'd bark.<br>  <br>  But 'mid those feminine and timorous men<br>  Intrepid that soft lady her fair front<br>  Advanc'd, and, "Who art thou, whose impious arm<br>  'Gainst royalty's anointed head dare sway<br>  Irreverent menace?" -- "One whom grinding wrong,<br>  And injuries savage, black, and manifold<br>  Have almost madden'd to the deep base shame [160]<br>  Of soiling his bright arms with woman's blood."<br>  (He cast the javelin from him, and went on)<br>  "But tell thy sire, Rowena, tell thy lord,<br>  Britons have yet to learn their codes of war,<br>  That yet fastidious vengeance will not slake [165]<br>  But on a worthy victim its deep thirst."<br>  <br>  Then was the mingling of their looks elate,<br>  As when two falcons, far from this low earth,<br>  Meet in the sun's broad blaze, they glad and proud<br>  Each of their kindred, flap their radiant wings. [170]<br>  <br>  "I know thee now, majestic Rebel!  thee<br>  The untraceable, untameable!  I know<br>  The chosen Man of Fate!  of all our race<br>  The designated danger; merciful<br>  Saxon ne'er coupled with thy name till now. [175]<br>  Yet think not thou from rivalry aloof<br>  In proud and lonely excellence to stand,<br>  For with requital royal and profuse<br>  I will outsoar thee; this white woman's hand<br>  Shall cast thee Hengist's pardon for thy deeds [180]<br>  Of guilty fame; this smooth and purple cheek<br>  Smile thee fair honours in Caer Merdhyn's court."<br>  <br>  "Pardon, and honour, Lady!  one alone<br>  Jealous prerogative of pardon holds<br>  O'er Samor's soul, the universal God! [185]<br>  Caer Merdhyn's honours!  to fall'n Vortigern<br>  To be install'd prime flatterer, meekly laud<br>  The bounteous-hearted monarch, who cast off<br>  His throne, his people, and his fame, and thought<br>  For bride so fair the dowry all too poor." [190]<br>  <br>  No wrath, but brighter joy the Lady's cheek<br>  Emblazon'd: "Why should slight and tinsel ties<br>  Of blood and birthplace hold asunder hearts<br>  Kindred in grandeur?  thou art brave and free,<br>  And brave and free is Hengist; why disdains [195]<br>  Valour to mate with valour, might with might?"<br>  "Valour beneath the sun goes proudly forth;<br>  And in the cloudy battle's van affronts<br>  His hauberk'd foe, but folds not secret steel<br>  Under the mild and festal robe of peace, [200]<br>  Nor creeps with midnight stealth on the weak sleep<br>  Of women and soft infants." -- Then appear'd<br>  Tears in her haughty eyes, tears beautiful,<br>  For drops of shame they were for those black crimes<br>  That fleck'd and dimm'd her father's blaze of fame. [205]<br>  Still paus'd not the Avenger. -- "Did my God,<br>  Did Britain claim the offering, I dare hope<br>  Yet I could rend from his worn heart away<br>  Its pleasant lust of vengeance; private wrongs<br>  Are but thin drops in my full tide of hate; [210]<br>  But all my country's injuries, all my God's<br>  Concentrate in the mighty passion flood,<br>  My life, my soul, my being; we must be,<br>  I and thy father, through all space of time,<br>  Even to the end, Destroyer or Destroy'd." -- [215]<br>  <br>  "Harsh and implacable!  yet be not thou<br>  Discourteous: wilt thou to Caer Merdhyn come,<br>  An honour'd guest, in freedom to depart<br>  When, where thou wilt, thy pledge my royal faith?"<br>  <br>  "A Saxon's faith!" burst bitter from his lips, [220]<br>  He check'd the upbraiding tone.  "If fraud and sin<br>  In such a lovely temple hold their shrine,<br>  It were not strange did fiends of darkness dwell<br>  Within yon beauteous sun!"  But she with smile<br>  Mild as May morning on a violet bank,<br>  "Why stayst thou?  can the Unconquerable fear --?"<br>  "Fear, Lady!  fear and I are strangers now." --<br>  "What wondrous spell," pursued her playful mirth,<br>  "So steels thee?" -- "One most simple and most strong,<br>  A calm proud conscience, and a faith in God." [230]<br>  <br>  Then sate he by the Lady's side; set forth<br>  Upon its dancing voyage down the tide<br>  The bark obeisant to its dashing oars.<br>  But those gay rowers veering with the wind<br>  Of soft court favour, 'gan with subtle joy [235]<br>  And cold factitious transport hail again<br>  Their gentle peer, their old and honour'd friend.<br>  But with a glance the imperial Lady froze<br>  To silence their smooth-lying lips, nor brook'd<br>  Idle instrusion on her rapturous feast. [240]<br>  Deep drank she in the majesty and pomp,<br>  Wherewith instinct the Avenger mov'd and spake,<br>  And what high beauty from heroic soul<br>  Emanates on the outward shape, nor pall'd<br>  On her insatiate appetite the joy;<br>  Till that commercing deep of stately thoughts,<br>  Proud admiration, and intense delight<br>  In what is heart-subliming, towering, grand,<br>  Regenerate from the trance that bath'd her sense,<br>  Sprang up a fiery passion, o'er her flow'd [250]<br>  Secret the intoxicating extacy,<br>  Love, dangerous, deep, intolerable love.<br>  <br>  What beauteous seeming and magnificent,<br>  Weareth that brilliant sin!  now not o'er her<br>  Came it in melting languor, soft and bland, [255]<br>  But like her own high nature, eminent,<br>  Disdainful, and elate, allied to all<br>  That beautified, that glorified, and seem'd<br>  Mysterious union of upsoaring spirits,<br>  Wedding of lofty thoughts with lofty thoughts, [260]<br>  And the fine joy of being to this earth<br>  A thing of wonder: and as floats the air<br>  Clear, white, and stainless in the highest heavens,<br>  Seem'd from its exaltation fresh and pure,<br>  Above all taint her amorous madness rose. [265]<br>  Had it seem'd love, her very pride had quell'd<br>  The umplum'd phantasy, her inbred scorn<br>  Warr'd on the young infirmity, but now<br>  Upon her soul's bold crest it planted high<br>  Its banner of dominion, and she hail'd [270]<br>  Its coming as a guest of pomp and power.<br>  <br>  But, though o'er all her features mantling spread<br>  A vivid restlessness, a lustrous glow,<br>  A deepening purple, though her eye indulg'd<br>  Richer delirium, though her languid breath [275]<br>  Came with a throb and struggle from her heart,<br>  Yet in that noble kindness that disdains<br>  With greedy and suspicious gaze to seach<br>  The sin that may be, rather chastening all<br>  With his own native purity, serene [280]<br>  The Warrior sate.  The placid gliding bark,<br>  With motion like to stillness, flowing on,<br>  Where with green diadem of woods above,<br>  Beneath the white breadth of the expanding stream,<br>  Caer Merdhyn in the liquid noontide rose. [285]<br>  <br>  Fair rose Caer Merdhyn, rose her towery height<br>  The air enriching, nor mis-seem'd a King<br>  Such stately dwelling; populous her streets,<br>  And throng'd with human faces, but o'er all<br>  A lassitude and heavy sadness hung, [290]<br>  Blankness of looks and weariness of hearts,<br>  And listlessness of motion faltering on.<br>  With all the pomps, the luxuries of life,<br>  It seem'd a city of the dead.  The shapes,<br>  The steps of men were there, but soul and spirit, [295]<br>  And stirring energy, and vivid mind,<br>  Passion and earnestness in torpor slept,<br>  The cold blood stagnate in the drowsy veins:<br>  Alike all feelings lazy languor seal'd.<br>  To still them, not delight, the mothers held [300]<br>  Their infants, as the radiant Queen past on;<br>  But even in them the laughing spring of joy<br>  Was dead, and dry, and frozen. -- "Oh, high God!<br>  (So spake the Wanderer in his secret soul)<br>  Hath tyranny such bleak and withering power [305]<br>  Man's heavenly essence to embrute, and thou,<br>  Once princely Vortigern, the tyrant thou!" --<br>  <br>  Worse sight! worse shame! they reach the broad hill's brow,<br>  Where in its royalty the palace look'd<br>  Awe on its vassal city; there, even there, [310]<br>  On that high threshold, armed Saxon files<br>  From the weak people fenc'd the weaker King.<br>  But through that legion hateful and accurst<br>  Onward the Avenger that bright Lady's hand<br>  Led, as the Sybil sage the Love-queen's son [315]<br>  Calm through the doleful regions of the dead.<br>  <br>  Within the hall with royal banners hung,<br>  And shields of royal blazon, royal arms,<br>  Least royal he, sate Vortigern; deep thought<br>  And miserable on his faded brow [320]<br>  Traced its bleak lines, before him glittering lay<br>  The crown of Britain, which his eye perused<br>  With a sick sadness, as each gem were full<br>  Of woeful ruminations, blank remorse;<br>  And as bad Angels loathe, yet upward watch, [325]<br>  Heaven's Sun, bright type of their once radiant state,<br>  Even so in bitterness that fallen King,<br>  Painfully banquetting on self-reproach,<br>  A drear remembrance of lost grandeurs drew<br>  From that fair ring, and curs'd its blaze that flash'd [330]<br>  Past splendours o'er the darkness of his soul,<br>  And memory from what height to what depth sunk,<br>  He welters in the abyss of shame profound.<br>  Beside him o'er his harp Aneurin bow'd,<br>  The white-hair'd Bard, sole faithful he, sole friend; [335]<br>  For minds of poets from their own high sphere<br>  Look down on earth's distinctions, high and low,<br>  Sunken or soaring, as the equal sun<br>  Sheds light along the vale and mountain's brow.<br>  He in the hall of feasting who fast seal'd [340]<br>  The treasures of his harmony, now pours<br>  Into the wounded heart his syrups sweet,<br>  And laps it in the silken folds of sound.<br>  But even along his strings the infectious grief<br>  Hath crept, and wither'd up their wantonness. [345]<br>  And wayward wanderings of despair belate<br>  His fickle tones: anon bursts full and free<br>  A start, a swell of pride, then sinks away<br>  Involuntary to such doleful fall,<br>  Misery so musical, its languid breath [350]<br>  Feeds, while it softens the deep-rooted woe.<br>  Such melodies at tragic midnight heard<br>  'Mid a deserted city, gliding o'er<br>  The deep green moss of tower and fane o'erthrown,<br>  Had seem'd immortal sorrows in the air, [355]<br>  O'er man's inconstant grandeurs.  Sad such wreck,<br>  More sad, more worthy Angels woe the waste<br>  And desolation of a noble mind,<br>  High fertile faculties run wild and rank,<br>  Bright fiery qualities in darkness slaked. [360]<br>  That liquid intercourse of grief broke off,<br>  Thus spake the King -- "Who thus unbidden bursts<br>  On kingly solitude?  why ask I thee?<br>  No brow between the Scot and Southern sea<br>  Beareth such gallant insolence abroad, [365]<br>  But Samor, the wild Wanderer, the denounc'd,<br>  The desperate!  Art thou here to stun mine ears<br>  With "Vortigern is abject, lost, disgrac'd?"<br>  'Tis well that with thee comes by bright excuse,<br>  My poverty's rich treasure, my night's star, [370]<br>  Beauteous Rowena." -- Joy seem'd his, but yet<br>  Was effort and was struggle in that joy,<br>  The clinging of a desperate soul to what<br>  It would delight in, but did not delight,<br>  The striving of a barren heart to force [375]<br>  The perish'd bloom of pleasure, -- "King, I come<br>  To put a spell upon thee, conjure up<br>  Thy valour from its tomb within thy breast,<br>  To rend the adamant that trammels fast<br>  Thy strength of soul.  By yon bright glaive that smote<br>  By Esk's wild bank, beneath his father's shield, [381]<br>  The royal Caledonian's son; yon flag,<br>  That, when by fated Arles rash Britain lost<br>  Her wild bright hazard for imperial state,<br>  Clouding the car of adverse victory shook [385]<br>  Untarnish'd in the sun its blazon broad,<br>  Nor stoop'd, though all was fallen; by yon rich crown,<br>  Whereon when flow'd the holy oil, this isle<br>  From all her seas her gratulant acclaim<br>  Sent up, and overcast heaven's vault with joy; [390]<br>  By Vortigern, the great, the brave, the wise! --<br>  "Brave! wise! aye, that it is.  The veriest wretch<br>  That from the base birth-place to his baser grave,<br>  Creeps with his fellow reptiles, that ne'er knew<br>  What luxury 'tis, what loftiness to soar, [395]<br>  And with one soul to wield a host of souls<br>  In free subjection, oh that fireless dust,<br>  Clay uninform'd, that only lives to die,<br>  That is to me a God: to me whose curse,<br>  And brand, and mock it is to have been great -- [400]<br>  And be -- oh! Samor, Samor, I was King,<br>  King of this spacious, rich, and glorious isle,<br>  And thou, and such as thou, my regal state<br>  Didst vassal; now, but now an eye may trace<br>  The circuit of my realm, a shepherd's boy [405]<br>  Count my thin people, like his mountain flock."<br>  <br>  "Oh, Monarch, ill must be atoned by good,<br>  And to repentant deeds of mightiest fame<br>  Heaven can upraise the farthest sunken.  Power<br>  Fails not the aspirant will.  I knew thee once [410]<br>  A being of those arduous energies,<br>  Strong aspirations, graspings undefin'd,<br>  Tumultuous thirsts and passions, that of man<br>  Make Fiend or Angel." -- "True, too true, but thou<br>  Hast seiz'd the Seraph's air-plum'd wings, and I [415]<br>  The Demon's vans of darkness.  Had all fallen,<br>  All perish'd, one wide ignominy swept<br>  Princes and Lords and People, I had found<br>  A forlorn comfort in the general wreck;<br>  But in its curst sublimity thy fame [420]<br>  Obtrudes its radiant presence, and makes groan<br>  This ruin of a Monarch." -- "Rare it is,<br>  Oh King, in Fame's rich galaxy to shine<br>  With stedfast blaze unwithering, but to dawn<br>  From darkness, scatter off the black eclipse [425]<br>  That veils the wither'd lustre, this most rare,<br>  Maketh man's soul an everlasting fire<br>  Worthy the God that hung the Heavens with light;<br>  'Tis hard for downcast spirit to o'erleap<br>  Ruin's sad barriers, but Heaven's angels drop [430]<br>  Soft dews beneath his burning feet, his flight<br>  Imp with strong plumes; his coming doth adorn<br>  The earth he moves on; till Remorse abash'd<br>  Before the orient glories fades and flies." --<br>  <br>  "Peace! peace! thou canst not see what cold within<br>  Lies like a palsy on the flagging powers, [436]<br>  Makes me a thin and shrinking reed, the sport<br>  Of every lazy wind, the shape, the life,<br>  The woe, without the faculties of man,<br>  Shame, shame. -- Oh, turn thy lofty brow away, [440]<br>  Heavy it hangs o'er me like loosen'd crag<br>  Over the mountain traveller -- I endure,<br>  Of all this nation, the curse-wrinkled lips,<br>  Out-pointed fingers, ribald jests, coarse scorns.<br>  Men that have lick'd the dust beneath my feet, [445]<br>  Worn their tame faces by the mould of mine,<br>  Them, to confront even them." -- Unkingly tears<br>  Chok'd the full utterance, met his eye the glance<br>  Of that proud Queen, who, all unmark'd, drank in<br>  That passionate discourse, from her contempt, [450]<br>  Though far below his own, he shrunk, and wrought<br>  To a brief pride his wan dejected mien.<br>  "Here is my throne, my kingdom is this breast,<br>  My diadem the wealth of light that shines<br>  From yon fair brow upon me." -- Stronger pain [455]<br>  Burst in upon the infant pride; forth fled<br>  The Monarch, happy could he fly himself.<br>  Him follow'd that old Bard.  "'Tis vain, all vain,<br>  (Thus spake the high Avenger.) "Beauteous Queen,<br>  I claim thy faith, and part." -- "So swift, so soon, [460]<br>  Our festal cheer untasted, welcome cup<br>  Uncrown'd?" -- "Fair Queen, in the pellucid stream<br>  My beverage dances; the coarse mountain boor<br>  Shares his hard fare with me; the hand that feasts<br>  The winged wanderers of the air, feasts me." -- [465]<br>  <br>  With lips in act of speech apart, the Queen,<br>  As to her will her tongue didainful scorn'd<br>  Allegiance, chain'd in silence stood again.<br>  Twice she essay's to speak, twice o'er her shame<br>  Swept his petrific hand, and rosy fire [470]<br>  O'er face and neck and forehead flush'd, till shrunk<br>  From that strong heat the eye, and down on earth<br>  Settled its close-fring'd orb; with pressure soft<br>  Her blushing fingers his bronz'd hand embrac'd.<br>  <br>  "Here in this palace is my rule, this land [475]<br>  Is mine by my prevailing power, would'st thou<br>  Of this high seat, this realm be Lord? -- Why starts<br>  Unwonted colour to thy cheek? why shrinks<br>  Into its sphere thine eye?  Said I this soul<br>  And what soft beauty glitters in this shape, [480]<br>  Had it appall'd thee? -- Eagerly she grasp'd<br>  The hand she held, as though from thence to wring<br>  A swift reply, yet gaz'd upon the earth,<br>  As wistful 'neath its darkness she might shrink<br>  From her own shame.  Blank wonder Samor's brow [485]<br>  To living stone congeal'd -- "This then the close<br>  To all thy lavish love of Vortigern!"<br>  <br>  "My love!  he was a King, upon his brow<br>  The beauty of a royal crown, his height<br>  Dominion, like a precious mantle, dipt [490]<br>  In heaven's pure light array'd, and o'er him flung<br>  Transcendant grandeur; above all he stood,<br>  And I by such fond splendours wooed and won,<br>  Took seat upon his eminence; a plant<br>  To spread, and mantle an imperial throne, [495]<br>  Not like tame ivy round a ruin creep,<br>  Or wreathe the tomb of royalty.  His pride<br>  I wedded, not his shame; bats may not build<br>  With the light-loving lark.  He, he himself<br>  By self-abasement has divorc'd me, set [500]<br>  Distance between us wide and far as heaven<br>  From the black pit of infamy." -- "High Queen,<br>  What seest thou in this bleak and batter'd brow,<br>  These rough scath'd limbs, this wan and sunken face,<br>  With misery's rugged furrows deeply plough'd, [505]<br>  To dazzle or delight?  Lone outcast I, <br>  Friendless, but daily, nightly by fierce foes<br>  Beset and hunted like a loathsome brute;<br>  Thy nation's mothers vent all hate on me,<br>  Link with a scathing curse no name but mine. [510]<br>  Oh, what would'st thou and softness with a life<br>  Like mine so dreary, desperate, dark, and fierce?<br>  <br>  "Oh, 'tis because all hate thee, that I love,<br>  Because all dread thee, I would mate with thee,<br>  Thy miseries, thy dangers deeper drown [515]<br>  My soul with passion, that thou walk'st alone,<br>  Smote at by every arm, yet struck by none,<br>  That mastery of thy single soul holds down<br>  The Saxons mounting empire, clips its wings<br>  Rapacious and wide-shadowing, that thy fame [520]<br>  Like a rich rainbow cloud, sails on through air,<br>  To mortal grasp impalpable, to sight<br>  In lonely brilliance manifest; my soul<br>  To that thy airy chariot would aspire,<br>  And dazzle by thy side, and daunt the world." -- [525]<br>  <br>  "Loose and unrighteous to thy lawful Lord,<br>  Yet would'st thou poison with adulterous shame<br>  Its spotless lustre, its pure white defile,<br>  And clog with guilt its vaunted wheels." -- Guilt! Guilt!<br>  Ah, now I know why mine eye shrunk from thine, [530]<br>  Why sought the base earth, why brook'd not my tongue<br>  The motions of my will -- but we -- shrink we?<br>  The lofty are their own high law; dull codes,<br>  Cold customs, trammel but the base; our sins<br>  Shall be the wanderings of the meteor fire, [535]<br>  More wonder'd than the regular calm stars:<br>  Our acting shall ennoble, what tame tongues<br>  Falter at even in word, opinions hues<br>  Shall at our haughty bidding shift and change,<br>  And what we do, shall therefore be call'd great. [540]<br>  Yes, yes, I feel thy shrinking hand, I see<br>  White-lipp'd abhorrence quivering in thy mien<br>  As at some loathsome viper.  Woe, oh woe<br>  To him that tramples on the viper's wrath." --<br>  Then shook she back her golden hair, away [545]<br>  Cast his cold hand. -- "Ho, Saxons at the gate,<br>  Ho, Saxons, to your injured Queen!"  The hall<br>  Sudden was walled with fiery arms and spears<br>  Bickering fierce menace; numerous, swift, and strong,<br>  As when old Cadmus by clear Dirce spread [550]<br>  That dangerous seed uncouth, long, wide, and bright<br>  Under the fatal ploughshare leap'd to life,<br>  To havock the wild harvest, and shook up<br>  Its bearded grim fertility of death.<br>  <br>  But then his sword the Avenger grasp'd, and cried,<br>  "Twice have I trusted Saxon faith, and twice [556]<br>  Beneath my feet the smooth fair ice hath burst<br>  Its glassy treachery: once this arm redeem'd<br>  The infatuate blindness.  Saxons, I am he<br>  Who with his single strength on Ambri plain [560]<br>  Scared your hot massacre, your proudest necks<br>  Strew'd for his pavement of retreat, ye see<br>  Mine arm unwither'd; yet unbroken sword."<br>  <br>  But they sprung onward; that bright Lady's brow<br>  Awful delight absorb'd the while, she moved [565]<br>  Before their wrath, her arm's high sway wav'd back<br>  Their fury from her presence.  Swift they came,<br>  Swift they departed; silence down the walls<br>  Crept o'er the banners broad, and pendant shields.<br>  <br>  She look'd on Samor, all his pride was hers, [570]<br>  She look'd on Samor, all that pride was quench'd<br>  In exquisite mild transport; at his feet<br>  The Queen, the haughty, the disdainful fell.<br>  Her fine fair hair lay floating on the earth;<br>  Her round arms clung beseeching to his knees. [575]<br>  <br>  "A curse upon me, that my wilful heart<br>  'Gainst head so brave, so noble, dream'd of wrath,<br>  Of danger and rude menace.  What I did,<br>  I know not, what I said, it pleased not thee,<br>  Enough, 'twas base, 'twas criminal, 'twas false. [580]<br>  Oh Chief! when we would compass wild desires,<br>  Words alien to the heart start up, yet seem,<br>  Most strong persuasion; of all serpents, scorn<br>  Stings to worse frenzy, worst a woman's soul.<br>  Forget, all, all forget, but one soft word, [585]<br>  And that I charge thee, by thy rescued life,<br>  Forget not." -- "Lady, were I rich in love,<br>  As yon full Sun in light, I could not spare<br>  A beam upon a Saxon.  Now, but now<br>  The fountains of my heart are dry, the stock [590]<br>  Where fresh and rich my green affections bloom'd,<br>  Is wither'd to the root; hard, doleful, dead,<br>  My breast's impassive iron scatters off<br>  All melting blandishments, all soft delights,<br>  As the wav'd banner the thin morning dews. [595]<br>  With one harsh discord to consummate all;<br>  Thou art thy Father's daughter." -- She arose<br>  In miserable calmness resolute.<br>  She took his hand, she led him forth, beneath<br>  The murky scowling of those Saxons stern, [600]<br>  Whose angry wonder scarce herself controll'd:<br>  Gave one fond lingering pressure, and but one,<br>  Then watch'd him through the city, up the vale,<br>  If gazing with such emptiness of eye<br>  Were watching, which his distance seem'd to freeze [605]<br>  Gradual to hollower wanness; down her arms<br>  Hung, only that she stood and faintly breath'd,<br>  Pulse, motion, sense, life, all seem'd fled with him.<br>  <br>  Sudden above her, the mild air 'gan waft<br>  Wild fiery sounds, like those of battle morn, [610]<br>  Which champing war-steed's neigh, and lance's rush,<br>  Impatient answers.  On the palace top<br>  Aneurin in his bardic glory stood;<br>  The sunlight on his old prophetic brow<br>  Flash'd strong, yet dazzled not, his long white locks [615]<br>  Stream'd back upon his azure robe, like rack<br>  O'er heaven's unclouded blue, his pale thin hand<br>  With strength of mounting phrenzy launch'd abroad<br>  The war-song of Cassivelan: glad sounds<br>  To that tranc'd queen, for Samor's hastier port [620]<br>  Deliberate grandeur slacken'd, he look'd back,<br>  Proud gratitude for that wild flattery. -- "All,<br>  All in one wide conspiracy, (so spake<br>  Rowena's bitter joy) thee, only thee<br>  To glorify.  Oh, were man mute, this earth [625]<br>  Would leap to utterance of thy fame, the winds<br>  Find voices eloquent, the streams, the stones,<br>  To lofty music burst of thy renown."<br>  <br>  Slowly retired the Queen; she call'd around<br>  Her slaves, her handmaids; arrogant their looks [630]<br>  Seem'd to confront her, eyes aye wont to shrink<br>  Before her gaze, now seem'd to pry and pierce<br>  Her deepest soul's recesses; and she blush'd<br>  Even in her plenitude of scorn.  They stood<br>  Trembling before her wayward mood, yet seem'd [635]<br>  Mockeries their tremors; solitude she sought,<br>  Yet solitude found none, things senseless took<br>  Stern cognizance of all her acts, her thoughts:<br>  Eyes hung the empty walls, weak laughing sounds<br>  Of triumph o'er her shame, pervaded wide [640]<br>  The tranquil air, all with herself at league<br>  Shook scorns upon herself.  Dim evening falls,<br>  O'er earth and sky, slow flits the shadowy night.<br>  "Slaves there!" she cried, "my steed! alone I ride."<br>  She wont to find her every look a law, [645]<br>  Now almost wonders all so swift obey.<br>  <br>  The moon's white sickle tenderly array'd<br>  With dubious lustre the gray heavens; scarce tinged<br>  The dew-webs, whiten'd not the yellow crown<br>  Of the unwaving forest; ignorant, [650]<br>  Or with feign'd ignorance 'guiling even herself,<br>  Long upon Samor's track the Lady rides.<br>  <br>  'Tis not a stag that couches on the heath;<br>  Hope on her dim cheek brightens, from her steed<br>  Soft she dismounts, she ruffles not the fern, [655]<br>  The moss springs printless up beneath her feet,<br>  So light her gliding to that slumbering man.<br>  She knows him, she starts back. -- "Oh, came I here,<br>  Lost and abas'd, him, only him to seek,<br>  That answers mine immodest heart with flight, [660]<br>  With scorn, perchance with hate!  yet wonderous he,<br>  Wonderous in rest as action!  Sleep'st thou calm,<br>  While numberless as these brown heath-spikes rise<br>  Legions of spears around thee, for thy blood<br>  Leagued in one furious thirst?  Unwise and rash! [665]<br>  To night thou slumber'st not unguarded, sleep;<br>  And if Rowena mingle with thy dreams,<br>  Sleep calmly, breathingly as now!  He wakes --<br>  Oh, hateful even in slumber that harsh name<br>  Grates on his sense." -- His eyes unfold, nor start, [670]<br>  So soft the vision; wonder's self is calm,<br>  And quaffs it in with mild unshrinking gaze.<br>  Her long bright hair, like threads of silver streak<br>  The moonlight, her fair forehead's marble arch<br>  Wild joyous fearfulness, extatic doubt, [675]<br>  Bathe with the dewyness of melting snow,<br>  Ere yet unblanch'd its stainless glitter pure.<br>  Oh, soft and slow that melody of mien<br>  Steals o'er the slumberer, ere the reason woke,<br>  The sense was drunken, one hand folded her's [680]<br>  That answer'd not its pressure, nor withdrew,<br>  Tremulous, yet motionless: his rising head<br>  Found on her other arm such pillowing soft,<br>  As the fond ringdove on its mate's smooth down.<br>  They spake not, moved not. 'Tis the noon of night, [685]<br>  Hour known to Samor not by sign or sound<br>  Of man's wise art to mark the fleeting time,<br>  Nor changing of the starry heavens; but e'er<br>  By motion of the secret soul, by calm<br>  Habitual sliding into the sooth'd heart, [690]<br>  Distinct from turbulent day and weary eve,<br>  Emeric's own hour, her consecrated spot<br>  In his life's wilderness.  She comes, she comes,<br>  The clouds have dropt her from their silvery folds;<br>  The mild air wafts her, the rank earth impure [695]<br>  Stainless she skims, distrust, doubt, fear, no place<br>  Find in the sinless candour of her mien.<br>  In languid soft security she melts<br>  On Samor's fever'd soul, she fills his sense,<br>  Her softness like the nightingale's first notes [700]<br>  After rude evening, o'er his passion steals:<br>  He cast not off Rowena's hand, it fell<br>  As from a dead man's grasp; slow rose his head<br>  From its fair zone, as from a bank of snow<br>  The winter traveller, by its smoothness guil'd [705]<br>  Almost to deathful sleep; he dares not now<br>  Welcome that heavenly visitant, nor could,<br>  Nor would he her mild rescue bid depart.<br>  Nor dares he now with chill abhorrence shrink<br>  From that empassion'd Lady; on his lips [710]<br>  Clung wretched, pale, beseechingness, that framed<br>  Nor word nor sound.  But time for thought in her<br>  Gave time for shame, for struggling pride gave time.<br>  "Thou deem'st me loose, wild, wanton, deem'st me come<br>  To lure thee with light sweets of lawless love, [715]<br>  Hunting mine own shame through the midnight woods.<br>  Oh false, all false. -- How thee shall I persuade,<br>  Aye me!  that scarce persuade myself, 'twas chance,<br>  'Twas fate, 'twas ministration of bad spirits,<br>  That led me thoughtless, hopeless -- did I say [720]<br>  Hopeless?  yet scorn not thou, the lightest won<br>  Are oft best won.  Oh why, ere now so mild,<br>  So gentle, why so stern, so ghastly still?"<br>  "Thou love'st my pride, my honour, my renown.<br>  Now, Queen Rowena, may'st thou do a deed [725]<br>  Shall make my pride thine own, make thee my fount<br>  Of honour, all my noontide of renown<br>  On thee in all its golden brilliance shine;<br>  And if henceforth man's voice cry out, High deeds<br>  Hath Samor's arm achiev'd, thy heart shall bound [730]<br>  And thy lips answer, 'Mine! all mine!' and I<br>  Will bless thee, thank thee, praise thee for that truth."<br>  <br>  O'er proud Rowena past his solemn voice<br>  Tremendously delightful, as the sound<br>  Of thunder over Jove's bold-minist'ring bird, [735]<br>  That sternly rocks on th'agitated air.<br>  "Speak, speak, 'tis hours, 'tis years until 'tis done."<br>  Return'd one brief, one powerful word -- "Depart."<br>  She struggled yet to wear the lofty light<br>  That flush'd her brow, she struggled, and she fell [740]<br>  Her white arms round his neck.  Light as the breeze<br>  Pass'd over his her cheek.  Then back<br>  She started, seiz'd her courser's rein; far, far<br>  The rocks gave answer to its trampling hoofs.<br>  <br>  To solitude, to peace, ah, not to peace! [745]<br>  Was Samor left; large dewy beads distil<br>  From his full brow, as from the forest leaves<br>  The sunny icicle: fierce, merciless,<br>  Relentless inquest o'er himself he holds,<br>  In him a sin in thought is sin in deed. [750]<br>  <br>  "And I, that on the frantic waxen wings<br>  Of mine own arrogance, have deem'd my soul<br>  Kindred and heritor of that rich bliss<br>  That bathes the Angels radiant wings in strength,<br>  That wander'd o'er this sublunary wild [755]<br>  As with a charter'd scorn, that mix'd with men<br>  But in disdainful mastery to o'er-rule<br>  Their dim and wavering destinies, that took<br>  With noble violence admiring earth,<br>  O'er me hath passion wound her silken nets; [760]<br>  And that soft Dalila, lascivious sin,<br>  Shorn my full honours.  Now, who clothed my steps<br>  With darkness, dread, and danger, hung my arms<br>  With light'ning, kept at bay the envious death<br>  That feasts upon the famous of mankind; [765]<br>  God, God abandons me.  So farewell pride,<br>  And with pride farewell strength, the burning hope,<br>  Glad agonies, brave bliss of holy war,<br>  Transports of trampling on my country's foes,<br>  And all the beauty, majesty, renown, [770]<br>  Vengeance, of thy triumphal state.  Ye too,<br>  Farewell, soft midnights, delicate regards<br>  Fix'd on me from fond eyes yet bright from heaven,<br>  Mild agitations of the purer sense,<br>  Fresh bloomings of my faded joys, ye dreams [775]<br>  Lovelier than actual bliss, as heaven than earth,<br>  Emeric abandons me.  For how can snow<br>  Drop on this foul earth stainless?  how canst thou<br>  Visit unsullied thy sad shrine defil'd,<br>  Or beam upon this lust-benighted heart? [780]<br>  Oh never felt before, the fear to front<br>  Mine own past life, the ignoble shame that burns<br>  At human sight, and memory that ne'er sleeps;<br>  Heart-sickening at its own deformities,<br>  A miserable welcome bid I ye, [785]<br>  Come, dismal comforters, faint-footed guides,<br>  Teach me the hate of life, the dread of death."<br>  <br>  And Samor wander'd on, not now with scope<br>  Resolv'd, and steady purpose that absorb'd<br>  And fix'd on one stern centre all his soul, [790]<br>  True as the arrow to its mark.  Now where,<br>  Whither, is all indifferent, he pursues<br>  The wildering of the forest track, the brook<br>  Winding its lucid error: two sad days<br>  And chance hath led him back to Wye's green bank. [795]<br>  <br>  Sudden before him swept in gallant pack,<br>  Fleet hounds, whose keen scent quaff'd the morning dews.<br>  Sole on their track a noble huntsman bow'd<br>  O'er his steed's high-curv'd neck.  But when he saw<br>  Samor, that scarce his coming mark'd or heard, [800]<br>  He vaulted from his uncheck'd steed so fleet,<br>  The courser seem'd to feel it not, but on<br>  Went stately bounding down the glen.  But he<br>  Unslung his bugle horn, his hunting spear<br>  Cast to the winds, and held his burnish'd sword [805]<br>  To heaven, as though to paragon its light.<br>  <br>  "Oh, thunderer Thor, but one bold prayer of mine<br>  E'er scaled thy heavens, and that, munificent,<br>  I thank thee for thy granting.  Samor now,<br>  Now Christian, now baptiz'd in German blood, [810]<br>  Avenger, we are met, and ere we part,<br>  Earth must be ruddier with some blood of ours."<br>  <br>  "Noble Argantyr, deem not thou unknown<br>  Thy name, thy presence, nor forgot, how thou,<br>  When Murther quaff'd his glut on Ambri plan, [815]<br>  Didst hold thy jealous steel aloft, lest stain<br>  From gore by treason shed, should dim its gleam;<br>  And when I burst my iron toils, and won<br>  My dangerous safety, how indignant joy<br>  Stood bathing thy stern brow.  Brave Anglian, thou, [820]<br>  But thou, of German race, to faint sloth chill'st<br>  My sword's quick wrath." -- "What, Samor out of love<br>  With strife, with music of conflicting steel?<br>  Hath Abisa's pale blood so quench'd his fire?<br>  Were't not I now could force my glorious will, [825]<br>  Yea, I could sue thee, Briton, for the joy.<br>  Thou wilt not credit, air hath been defil'd<br>  With creeping whispers cold, that I, I shrunk<br>  To second in his dangers that brave boy,<br>  As though Argantyr would partake a foe, [830]<br>  And with division spiritless and base,<br>  Mete out his province in one man to slay,<br>  Hear; 'Well the famous Anglian won his half<br>  Of that great conquest!'  But I have thee now<br>  Whole, undivided, now, or man, or more, [835]<br>  If aught be mortal in thee, guard that spot,<br>  My steel will search it," -- "Samor is not now<br>  As Samor was, but knows not yet to scorn<br>  Such brave allurements."  Forth his anlace flash'd,<br>  But not as wont, uplooks he to the sky; [840]<br>  He thinks not now, on, if I fall, float near,<br>  My Emeric, that no Angel's voice but thine<br>  Welcome thy Samor to his opening heaven:<br>  And if I vanquish, Britain and the Lord<br>  Take to your hecatomb one Saxon more. [845]<br>  <br>  But on Argantyr sprung, as wanton boy<br>  To the cool health of summer streamlet pure:<br>  Around, above, beneath his winged sword<br>  Leaps in its fiery joy, red, fierce and far<br>  As from a midnight furnace start the sparks. [850]<br>  As brazen statue on proud palace top,<br>  Shakes off the pelting tempest, so endur'd<br>  Samor, but not in patient hope austere<br>  Of victory; but habitual skill and power<br>  Protracting long the cold indifferent strife; [855]<br>  Till twice that sword that in its downward sweep<br>  Flash'd the white sunlight, cloudy rose and dim<br>  With ominous purple: then his nature burst<br>  Its languid bonds, not front alone to front;<br>  But soul to soul the riot of the fight [860]<br>  They mingle, like to giddy chariot wheels<br>  The whirling of their swords, as fierce the din<br>  Of buckler brast, helm riven, and breastplate cloven,<br>  As when the polar wind the ice field rends.<br>  Such nobleness sublime of hideous fight [865]<br>  From Ilion's towers her floating mantled dames<br>  Saw not, nor Thebes, when Capaneus call'd down<br>  Jove's thunder, and disdain'd its fall, nor pride<br>  Of later Bards, when mad Orlando met<br>  On that frail bridge the giant Sarzan king, [870]<br>  And with him in the boiling flood dash'd down,<br>  Till that fond eagerness, that brave delight<br>  O'erpower'd frail nature, breathless each, and each<br>  Careless, yet conscious of deep trenching wounds,<br>  For admiration paus'd, for hope, for power [875]<br>  To satiate the unwearying strong desire.<br>  <br>  Lo, the far hills Argantyr first descried<br>  Radiant with spearmen, and he cried, "Away,<br>  'Tis Hengist with his bloody bands, I know<br>  The motion of his crest; brave Chief, away." -- [880]<br>  "Away!  and leave Argantyr here to boast<br>  Samor hath fled him!" -- "Oh, we meet again;<br>  Thou art a quarry for the Gods, base lance<br>  Must ne'er vaunt blood of thine.  Argantyr spares<br>  But for himself such noble game.  Still here! [885]<br>  Froward and furious, if thou need'st must die,<br>  Why so must I; fell Hengist will not spare<br>  And inch of quivering life on all thy limbs.<br>  And I with such a jealous lust pursue<br>  A noble conquest o'er thee, I must shield [890]<br>  Thy life with mine, for my peculiar fame;<br>  Freely mine own death on the hazard cast<br>  For such a precious stake as slaying thee."<br>  <br>  As through dusk twilight stolen, love-breathless maid<br>  For interchange of gentle vows, by noise [895]<br>  Startled of envious footstep, chides away<br>  Her lingering youth, yet for his lingering loves,<br>  Till her fond force hath driven him from her side;<br>  So earnest the brave Anglian sued to flight<br>  Reluctant Samor; o'er his sword hilt bow'd, [900]<br>  Stood sorrowing for the wounds himself had made,<br>  That marr'd his speedier flight.  Anon approach'd<br>  Hengist, encircled by his state of spears,<br>  And bright Rowena by his side.  "But now<br>  Thy steed along our camp rush'd masterless, [905]<br>  Therefore we seek thee, Anglican.  How!  thou bleedst!<br>  And strange!  thy foeman bites not the red earth.<br>  What might hath scathless met Argantyr's steed?"<br>  <br>  "He, gasp'd he here in death, thy soul would dance,<br>  The Wanderer!" -- "He! he wars but on soft boys, [910]<br>  He dare not front Argantyr." -- "False, 'tis false!"<br>  Burst from Rowena; "he dares deeds our Gods<br>  Had shrunk from (Hengist's cloudy brow she mark'd),<br>  Or whence his proud claim to my father's hate?"<br>  "Where hath the Recreant fled?  Pursue, pursue!" [915]<br>  Cried Hengist. "Hast thou wings to cleave the air?<br>  Or windest the deep bosom of the earth,<br>  Thou may'st o'ertake.  Yet Samor is not now,"<br>  He said, "as Samor was; were Samor more,<br>  Earth and Argantyr had been wed erenow." [920]<br>  <br>  So spake the Anglian; leap'd Rowena's heart<br>  In hope, in shame, in anguish, in delight.<br>  "Oh, hath my softness sunk so deep to change<br>  Thy steadfast nature, yet thus chang'd, thy might<br>  Wrests honour from thy foeman's lips." -- "Oh now," [925]<br>  Laughing in baffled bitterness, exclaim'd<br>  The Saxon King, "now weave we softer nets<br>  To toil this dangerous Wanderer.  What say'st thou,<br>  Fair-ey'd Rowena, now thou hast cast off<br>  Thy fond, thy lovesick Vortigern? perchance [930]<br>  The sunshine of thy beauty might melt down<br>  This savage to a tame submissive slave."<br>  <br>  Rowena, whose proud look with beauteous awe<br>  Smote her beholders, wore her loveliness<br>  As though she gloried in its power; now close [935]<br>  Crowded o'er all her face her mantle's folds,<br>  That ill conceal'd the purple fire within.<br>  Then forward past they to the Saxon camp.<br>  <br>  But far by Wye's green marge had Samor fled,<br>  Till now the ebbing blood with short quick throb [940]<br>  Beat at his heart, his languid feet were clogg'd<br>  With the thick forest leaves, the keen air search'd<br>  With a cold thrill his wounds.  He falls, scarce sobs;<br>  "Merciful God, on this in all my life<br>  The sole, the single day I would not die." [945]<br>  Then faint, and sickly, an oppressive rest<br>  Seal'd sight and sense.  When sleep feel on him, eve<br>  Was gathering fast, but when he woke, more shot<br>  From the gray east her faint pellucid light.<br>  His blood was staunch'd, a soothing coolness lay [950]<br>  On his mild wounds, the rude arch of the boughs<br>  Seem'd woven with officious care to veil<br>  The bright Sun from his eyelids; the dry leaves<br>  Were gathered round him, like a feathery couch.<br>  He lay and listen'd, a soft step approach'd [955]<br>  Light as the wren along the unshaking spray,<br>  And o'er him lean'd a maiden pale, yet blithe<br>  With tinge of joy, that settled hue. -- "Is't thou,<br>  Gentle Myfanwy?"  "Blessings on thy waking;<br>  I long'd to tell thee what sweet dreams have sooth'd [960]<br>  My sorrows since we parted; in my sleep<br>  My parents came, and with them that fond youth,<br>  And they smil'd on him kindly.  Think'st thou God<br>  Can have such mercy on sins dark as mine?"<br>  "God's plenteous mercies on thee for thy care [965]<br>  Of me, sweet maiden." -- "Pardon me, oh thou,<br>  Heaven pardon me, when first I saw thee cold,<br>  Helpless, and bleeding, evil thoughts arose<br>  Of my poor Abisa's untimely death."<br>  <br>  But deeper meditation Samor's mind [970]<br>  Beset. "Almighty, truely thou ordain'st<br>  Wisdom from baby lips; what moral high<br>  Breathes in this simple maid's light-hearted smiles!<br>  And I, for wisdom fam'd, for pride of mind,<br>  Insulted with weak doubts thy infinite, [975]<br>  Illimitable goodness; she so soft,<br>  So delicate, so sinful and so sad,<br>  Springs on her airy plumes of hope to thee.<br>  Oh, were mine guilt of act not thought, the stain<br>  Thy fount of living mercy might efface." [980]<br>  He prest a kiss upon her cheek so pure<br>  Even Abisa had granted it. -- "Farewell,<br>  My kind preserver, cherish thou thy hope,<br>  As 'twere an infant fondling on thy breast."<br>  And fresh with hope, like gay stag newly bath'd, [985]<br>  Forth on his voyage lone the Avenger past.<br>  <br>  <br>  <h3 align="CENTER"><b> BOOK VIII.</b> </h3>   His path is 'mid the Cambrian mountains wild;<br>  The many fountains that well wandering down<br>  Plinlimmon's huge round side their murmurs smooth<br>  Float round him; Idris, that like warrior old<br>  His batter'd and fantastic helmet rears, [5]<br>  Scattering the elements wrath, frowns o'er his way<br>  A broad irregular duskiness.  Aloof<br>  Snowdon, the triple-headed giant, soars,<br>  Clouds rolling half way down his rugged sides.<br>  <br>  Slow as he trod amid their dizzy heights, [10]<br>  Their silences and dimly mingling sounds,<br>  Rushing of torrents, roar of prison'd winds;<br>  O'er all his wounded soul flow'd strength, and pride,<br>  And hardihood; again his front soar'd up<br>  To commerce with the skies, and frank and bold [15]<br>  His majesty of step his rugged path<br>  Imprinted.  So in old poetic faith<br>  Hyperion from his native Delian bowers,<br>  'Mid the rich music of those sisters nine,<br>  Walk'd the bright heights of Helicon, and shook [20]<br>  His forehead's clustering glories wide, and flush'd<br>  The smoothness of his fair immortal face<br>  With purple Godhead.  Whence, ye mountains, whence<br>  The spirit that within your secret caves<br>  Holds kindred with man's soul?  Is't that your pomp [25]<br>  Of exaltation, your aërial crowns<br>  In their heaven-scaling rivalry cast forth<br>  Bold sympathies of loftiness, and scorn<br>  Contagious?  or in that your purer air,<br>  Where fresh and virgin from its golden fount, [30]<br>  Lies the fine light at morning, or at eve<br>  Melts upward and resolves itself from earth,<br>  And with its last clear trembling round ye clings;<br>  The soul, unwound its coarse material chains,<br>  Basks in its own divinity, and feels [35]<br>  There in the verge and portal of the heavens,<br>  The neighbourhood of brighter worlds unseen?<br>  Where the blue Glasslyn hurries her fleet course<br>  To wanton on the yellow level sands,<br>  On either side in sheer ascent abrupt [40]<br>  The rocks, like barriers that in elder time<br>  Wall'd the huge cities of the Anakim<br>  Upblacken to the sky, whose tender blue<br>  With mild relief salutes th' o'erlabour'd sight.<br>  There on the scanty slippery way, that winds [45]<br>  With the stream's windings, Samor loiters on.<br>  But who art thou, that in the Avenger's path<br>  Standest in dark serenity?  what joy<br>  Instinct amid thy thick black locks reveals<br>  The full voluptuous quietude within? [50]<br>  Oh, Prophet! in thy wanderings wide and far<br>  Amid the pregnant hours of future time,<br>  Haply the form of Samor, disarray'd<br>  Calamity's sad vesture, hath appear'd<br>  In plenitude of glory.  Hence thine eye [55]<br>  With recognition glad and bright salutes<br>  The Man of Fate.  To earth that Prophet old<br>  Bow'd down, then look'd he on the waters dark,<br>  Then upward to the mountains. "Stony earth,<br>  Within thy secret bosom feel'st not thou [60]<br>  A wonderous presence? dwells not, thou blue stream,<br>  Under thy depth of waves a silent awe? --<br>  Yea, Snowdon, lift thou up in sternest pride<br>  Thy cloudy mantled brow; ye know him all,<br>  Ye know the Avenger." -- "Merlin, mock not thou [65]<br>  Thy fellow creature of the dust, the child<br>  Of sin and sorrow, with o'erlabour'd phrase.<br>  Abasing the immortal elements<br>  From their high calm indifference to sense<br>  Of our light motions.  Simple truth severe [70]<br>  Best seemeth aged lips; oh, holy famed<br>  And sage, how ill strong Wisdom's voice melts down<br>  To the faint chime of flattery." -- "Poor of pride!<br>  Feeble of hope!  thou seest thyself forlorn,<br>  An hunted wanderer in thy native land. [75]<br>  I see thee clad in victory and revenge,<br>  Thy glory sailing wide on all the winds,<br>  Beautiful with thy blessings at thy feet<br>  Thy own fair Britain, Fate so freely spreads<br>  Her mystic volume to my sight." -- "Oh, blind, [80]<br>  And ignorant as blind our insect race!<br>  The mole would count the sunbeams, the blind worm<br>  Search the hid jewels in the depths of earth,<br>  And man, dim dreamer, would invade the heavens,<br>  Self-seated in the Almighty's councils read [85]<br>  The secrets of Omniscience, yea, with gaze<br>  Familiar scruntinize the Inscrutable.<br>  I tell thee, Merlin, that the soul of man<br>  Is destiny on earth; God gave us limbs<br>  To execute, and intellect to will [90]<br>  Or good or evil, and his unseen Spirit<br>  Our appetites of holiness, else faint<br>  And wavering doth corroborate: hence man's prides,<br>  Man's glories, and man's virtues all are God's.<br>  If yet this heart unwearied may bear on, [95]<br>  Nor from its holy purpose faintly swerve,<br>  The Lord be prais'd, its fate is pride and joy.<br>  But if, and oh the peril!  it play false<br>  Its country's lofty hazard, shall it shift<br>  On wayward destiny its sloth and sin?
